As\n\t * such, if it is ever used for determining the identity of a node in\n\t * the cluster, then routing decisions and so on should be made the\n\t * same way as for REMOTE_NODE_ID. If we ever assign unique identities\n\t * to each node in the cluster, then we'll probably need to convert\n\t * the implementation here into a map to select any of the possible\n\t * identities. But for now, this is good enough to capture the notion\n\t * of 'remote nodes in the cluster' for routing decisions.\n\t *\n\t * Remote nodes may also have, instead, an identity allocated from the\n\t * remote node identity scope, which is identified by the top 8 bits\n\t * being 0x02.\n\t *\n\t * Note that kube-apiserver policy is handled entirely separately by\n\t * the standard policymap enforcement logic and has no relationship to\n\t * the identity as used here. Policy enforcement maps\n- `/workspace/pkg/maps/ctmap/` - Connection tracking maps\n- `/workspace/pkg/maps/lxcmap/` - LXC/container endpoint maps\n- `/workspace/pkg/maps/nat/` - NAT mapping management\n- `/workspace/pkg/maps/lbmap/` - Load-balancer maps\n- `/workspace/pkg/maps/ipcache/` - IP-to-identity cache\n- `/workspace/pkg/maps/*/` - Individual map types\n\n---\n\n### **5. BPF Program Data Structures**\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/bpf/lib/common.h` and other headers\n\n**Core Structures:**\n\n```c\nstruct endpoint_key {\n    __u32 ip4;          // IPv4 address\n    __u32 family;       // Address family\n    __u32 key;          // Endpoint ID\n};\n\nstruct endpoint_info {\n    __u32 ifindex;      // Interface index\n    __u16 lxc_id;       // Endpoint ID\n    __u16 pad;\n    __u32 sec_label;    // Security identity\n    __u32 flags;\n    __u32 pad2;\n};\n\nstruct policy_key {\n    struct bpf_lpm_trie_key lpm_key;\n    __u32 sec_label;    // Source security identity\n    __u16 dport;        // Destination port\n    __u8 proto;         // Protocol (TCP, UDP, etc.)\n    __u8 egress;        // Direction (ingress=0, egress=1)\n};\n\nstruct policy_entry {\n    __u64 packets;\n    __u64 bytes;\n    __u32 proxy_port;\n    __u8 deny;          // Drop if set\n    __u8 auth_type;     // Auth requirement type\n    __u8 pad[6];\n};\n```\n\n---\n\n### **6. Tail Call Architecture**\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/bpf/include/bpf/tailcall.h` and `/workspace/bpf/lib/maps.h`\n\n**Mechanism:**\n- Uses BPF prog_array maps for dynamic program jumps\n- Two flavors:\n  1. `tail_call_static()` - Constant slot index (verified at compile time)\n  2. `tail_call_dynamic()` - Runtime-determined slot\n\n**Tail Call Slots** (from `bpf_lxc.c`):\n```\nCILIUM_CALL_DROP_NOTIFY (1)\nCILIUM_CALL_ERROR_NOTIFY (2)\nCILIUM_CALL_HANDLE_ICMP6_NS (4)\nCILIUM_CALL_SEND_ICMP6_TIME_EXCEEDED (5)\nCILIUM_CALL_ARP (6)\nCILIUM_CALL_IPV4_FROM_LXC (7)\nCILIUM_CALL_IPV6_FROM_LXC (10)\nCILIUM_CALL_IPV4_TO_LXC_POLICY_ONLY (11)\n... and many more\n```\n\n**Policy Enforcement Tail Calls:**\n- `POLICY_CALL_MAP` - Jump to per-endpoint ingress policy enforcement\n- `POLICY_EGRESSCALL_MAP` - Jump to per-endpoint egress policy enforcement\n\n---\n\n### **7. Integration with Kernel APIs**\n\n**Hook Attachment Points:**\n\n| Hook Type | Mechanism | Programs | Location |\n|-----------|-----------|----------|----------|\n| **TC Ingress** | TC qdisc | `cil_from_*` | Device ingress |\n| **TC Egress** | TC qdisc | `cil_to_*` | Device egress |\n| **XDP** | Driver/Generic | `cil_xdp_entry` | Physical NIC |\n| **Socket** | sk_msg/sk_skb | `bpf_sock.c` | Socket layer |\n| **Socket redir** | sk_msg_verdict | Redirects to proxy | User-space proxy |\n| **cgroup** | cgroup_sock_addr | Auth hooks | Namespace cgroup |\n\n**Key Kernel BPF Helpers Used:**\n- `bpf_map_lookup_elem()` - Map lookups\n- `bpf_tail_call()` - Program jumps\n- `bpf_perf_event_output()` - Event notifications\n- `bpf_redirect()` - Packet redirection\n- `bpf_get_current_pid_tgid()` - Process context\n- `bpf_probe_read()` - Kernel memory access\n- `bpf_clone_redirect()` - Packet cloning\n\n---\n\n### **8. Policy Enforcement Flow**\n\n**Ingress Flow (Container to External):**\n```\nbpf_lxc.c:cil_from_container\n  ↓\n[Identify source endpoint] → ENDPOINTS_MAP lookup\n  ↓\n[Extract security identity] → ipcache or endpoint_info\n  ↓\n[Lookup policy] → tail_call(CILIUM_CALL_IPV4_FROM_LXC)\n  ↓\n[Per-endpoint policy program] → POLICY_CALL_MAP[endpoint_id]\n  ↓\n[Check policy entry] → cilium_policy_* map (LPM match)\n  ↓\n[Enforce action] → allow/drop/redirect\n```\n\n**Egress Flow (External to Container):**\n```\nbpf_lxc.c:cil_to_container\n  ↓\n[Route to endpoint] → ENDPOINTS_MAP lookup by IP\n  ↓\n[Extract security identity] → destination identity\n  ↓\n[Lookup policy] → tail_call(CILIUM_CALL_IPV4_TO_LXC)\n  ↓\n[Per-endpoint policy program] → POLICY_CALL_MAP[endpoint_id]\n  ↓\n[Check policy entry] → cilium_policy_* map (LPM match)\n  ↓\n[Enforce action] → allow/drop/deliver\n```\n\n---\n\n### **9. Key Library Headers** (`/workspace/bpf/lib/`)\n\n| Header | Purpose |\n|--------|---------|\n| `common.h` | Core packet processing, data structures (~1K lines) |\n| `policy.h` | Policy lookup and enforcement (~250 lines) |\n| `nat.h` | SNAT/DNAT implementation (~1500 lines) |\n| `lb.h` | Load-balancing logic (~1500 lines) |\n| `conntrack.h` | Connection tracking (~1100 lines) |\n| `identity.h` | Security identity utilities |\n| `ipv4.h`, `ipv6.h` | IPv4/IPv6 processing |\n| `l3.h`, `l4.h` | Layer 3/4 processing |\n| `nodeport.h` | NodePort/ClusterIP handling (~2.4K lines) |\n| `egress_gateway.h` | Egress gateway implementation |\n| `host_firewall.h` | Host-level firewalling (~500 lines) |\n| `drop.h` | Drop reason categorization |\n| `trace.h` | Packet tracing/monitoring |\n| `encap.h` | Tunneling encapsulation |\n| `encrypt.h` | IPSec encryption |\n| `wireguard.h` | WireGuard integration |\n\n---\n\n### **10. Go-Level BPF Wrapper** (`/workspace/pkg/bpf/`)\n\n**Key Files:**\n\n**collection.go** - ELF parsing and program management\n- `LoadCollectionSpec(path)` - Load eBPF ELF file\n- Handles tail call annotation (`__section_tail`)\n- iproute2 compatibility for prog_arrays\n- Removes unreachable tail calls\n\n**map_linux.go** - Map operations (~1000 lines)\n```go\ntype Map struct {\n    m *ebpf.Map\n    key, value MapKey, MapValue\n    cache map[string]*cacheEntry\n    enableSync bool\n    withValueCache bool\n}\n```\n- Full map lifecycle management\n- Caching with sync retry\n- Per-CPU map support\n- Pressure metrics\n\n**bpffs_linux.go** - BPF Filesystem operations\n- Map pinning/unpinning\n- BPF object mounting\n- Path management\n\n**endpoint.go** - Per-endpoint BPF management\n- Endpoint-specific map names\n- Map cleanup on endpoint deletion\n\n---\n\n### **11. Endpoint Program Regeneration** (`/workspace/pkg/endpoint/`)\n\n**Flow:**\n\n1. **Trigger** - Policy change, endpoint creation/deletion\n2. **Context** - Create regeneration context with policies\n3. **Code Generation** - Generate endpoint-specific policy program\n4. **Compilation** - Compile via loader\n5. **Loading** - Load into kernel and attach to maps\n6. **Activation** - Update POLICY_CALL_MAP references\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `endpoint.go` - Core endpoint implementation (~2K lines)\n- `bpf.go` - eBPF integration\n- `policy.go` - Policy-to-eBPF conversion\n- `/workspace/pkg/endpoint/regeneration/` - Regeneration orchestration\n\n---\n\n### **12. Configuration System**\n\n**Header Files Generated at Runtime:**\n\n1. **`node_config.h`** - Node-level constants\n   - Node addresses, MTU, VXLAN endpoints\n   - Tunnel configuration\n   - Generated by `WriteNodeConfig()`\n\n2. **`netdev_config.h`** - Device-specific config\n   - Device names, MAC addresses\n   - Interface indices\n   - Generated by `WriteNetdevConfig()`\n\n3. **`filter_config.h`** - XDP filter configuration\n   - CIDR ranges for pre-filtering\n   - Generated by `WriteConfig()`\n\n4. **`ep_config.h`** - Per-endpoint config\n   - Endpoint ID, security identity\n   - Generated at endpoint regeneration time\n\n---\n\n### **13. Integration Points with Go Daemon**\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/pkg/datapath/types/` (interfaces)\n\nKey interfaces that coordinate datapath operations:\n- `CompilationLock` - Serialize concurrent compilations\n- `ConfigWriter` - Write configuration to disk\n- `NodeHandler` - Node-level datapath operations\n- `PreFilter` - XDP pre-filter configuration\n- `IptablesManager` - Host iptables management\n- `Proxy` - Layer 7 proxy integration\n\n---\n\n### **14. eBPF Program Entry Points**\n\n**From bpf_lxc.c:**\n\n1. Main entry: `__section_entry` (line 1443, 2281) - Packet ingress\n2. Tail calls to policy enforcement\n3. Multiple IPv4/IPv6 handling paths:\n   - IPv4 from container → IPv4 to container\n   - IPv6 from container → IPv6 to container\n   - ARP handling\n   - Per-packet load-balancing\n\n**Program Sections:**\n- Ingress path: ~1000 lines handling policy, NAT, LB\n- Egress path: ~1000 lines reverse path checking\n- Policy enforcement: ~600 lines with identity-based rules\n\n---\n\n### **Key Architectural Patterns**\n\n1. **Template + Specialization** - Common C library + per-endpoint policies\n2. **Tail Calls for Extensibility** - Policy programs loaded dynamically\n3. **Map-based Configuration** - Runtime reconfigurations without reload\n4. **Identity-based Policies** - Security identities decouple from IP addresses\n5. **Multi-level Caching** - Endpoint maps cache policy decisions\n6. **LPM Tries for Scalability** - Efficient CIDR matching\n7. **Per-CPU Maps** - Lock-free metrics and statistics\n\n---\n\nThis architecture provides a high-performance, flexible datapath that can handle complex network policies, load-balancing, NAT, and encryption all in the kernel with eBPF."},{"type":"text","text":"agentId: a654a558eb707d756 (for resuming to continue this agent's work if needed)\n<usage>total_tokens: 67684\ntool_uses: 55\nduration_ms: 96993</usage>"}]}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"16e5dfd3-7fda-4f16-8726-5227dd5f6343","uuid":"d2c188d0-d87e-4308-9561-3b6e316527a9","tool_use_result":{"status":"completed","prompt":"Explore the cilium/cilium codebase to understand the eBPF datapath subsystem architecture. `cil_from_container` - Ingress from pod\n  - `cil_to_container` - Egress to pod\n  - `cil_from_netdev` - Ingress from host device\n  - `cil_to_netdev` - Egress to host device\n  - `cil_from_host` - Ingress from host\n  - 142→\tif l.cfg.DeriveMasqIPAddrFromDevice != \"\" {\n   143→\t\tifName = l.cfg.DeriveMasqIPAddrFromDevice\n   144→\t}\n   145→\n   146→\taddrs := l.getNodeConfig().NodeAddresses\n   147→\n 238→\t// exclude devices that will still be managed going forward.\n   239→\tfor _, d := range devices {\n   240→\t\tif dev == d {\n   241→\t\t\treturn false\n   242→\t\t}\n   243→\t}\n   244→\n   245→\treturn true\n   246→}\n   247→\n   248→// removeObsoleteNetdevPrograms removes cil_to_netdev and cil_from_netdev from devices\n   249→// that cilium potentially doesn't manage anymore after a restart, e.g. if the set of\n   250→// devices changes between restarts.\n   251→//\n   252→// This code assumes that the agent was upgraded from a prior version while maintaining\n   253→// the same list of managed physical devices. This ensures that all tc bpf filters get\n   254→// replaced using the naming convention of the 'current' agent build. For example,\n   255→// before 1.13, most filters were named e.g. bpf_host.o:[to-host], to be changed to\n   256→// cilium-<device> in 1.13, then to cil_to_host-<device> in 1.14. As a result, this\n   257→// function only cleans up filters following the current naming scheme.\n   258→func removeObsoleteNetdevPrograms(devices []string) error {\n   259→\tlinks, err := safenetlink.LinkList()\n   260→\tif err != nil {\n   261→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"retrieving all netlink devices: %w\", err)\n   262→\t}\n   263→\n   264→\t// collect all devices that have netdev programs attached on either ingress or egress.\n   265→\tingressDevs := []netlink.Link{}\n   266→\tegressDevs := []netlink.Link{}\n   267→\tfor _, l := range links {\n   268→\t\tif !isObsoleteDev(l.Attrs().Name, devices) {\n   269→\t\t\tcontinue\n   270→\t\t}\n   271→\n   272→\t\t// Remove the per-device bpffs directory containing pinned links and\n   273→\t\t// per-endpoint maps.\n   274→\t\tbpffsPath := bpffsDeviceDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), l)\n   275→\t\tif err := bpf.Remove(bpffsPath); ok {\n   285→\t\t\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(bpfFilter.Name, symbolFromHostNetdevEp) {\n   286→\t\t\t\t\tingressDevs = append(ingressDevs, l)\n   287→\t\t\t\t}\n   288→\t\t\t}\n   289→\t\t}\n   290→\n   291→\t\tegressFilters, err := safenetlink.FilterList(l, directionToParent(dirEgress))\n   292→\t\tif err != nil {\n   293→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"listing egress filters: %w\", err)\n   294→\t\t}\n   295→\t\tfor _, filter := range egressFilters {\n   296→\t\t\tif bpfFilter, ok := filter.(*netlink.BpfFilter); On each retry, the\n   248→// log buffer quadruples in size, for a total of 5 attempts. If that proves\n   249→// insufficient, a truncated ebpf.VerifierError is returned.\n   250→//\n   251→// Any maps marked as pinned in the spec are automatically loaded from the path\n   252→// given in opts.Maps.PinPath and will be used instead of creating new ones.\n   253→// MapSpecs that differ (type/key/value/max/flags) from their pinned versions\n   254→// will result in an ebpf.ErrMapIncompatible here and the map must be removed\n   255→// before loading the CollectionSpec.\n   256→func LoadCollection(spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, opts *CollectionOptions) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error) {\n   257→\tif spec == nil {\n   258→\t\treturn nil, nil, errors.New(\"can't load nil CollectionSpec\")\n   259→\t}\n   260→\n   261→\tif opts == nil {\n   262→\t\topts = &CollectionOptions{}\n   263→\t}\n   264→\n   265→\t// Copy spec so the modifications below don't affect the input parameter,\n   266→\t// allowing the spec to be safely re-used by the caller.\n   267→\tspec = spec.Copy()\n   268→\n   269→\tif err := inlineGlobalData(spec, opts.Constants); err != nil {\n   270→\t\treturn nil, nil, fmt.Errorf(\"inlining global data: %w\", err)\n   271→\t}\n   272→\n   273→\t// Set initial size of verifier log buffer.\n   274→\t//\n   275→\t// Up until kernel 5.1, the maximum log size is (2^24)-1. In 5.2, this was\n   276→\t// increased to (2^30)-1 by 7a9f5c65abcc (\"bpf: increase verifier log limit\").\n   277→\t//\n   278→\t// The default value of (2^22)-1 was chosen to be large enough to fit the log\n   279→\t// of most Cilium programs, while falling just within the 5.1 maximum size in\n   280→\t// one of the steps of the multiplication loop below. Without the -1, it would\n   281→\t// overshoot the cap to 2^24, making e.g. verifier tests unable to load the\n   282→\t// program if the previous size (2^22) was too small to fit the log.\n   283→\tif opts.Programs.LogSize == 0 {\n   284→\t\topts.Programs.LogSize = 4_194_303\n   285→\t}\n   286→\n   287→\t// Find and strip all CILIUM_PIN_REPLACE pinning flags before creating the\n   288→\t// Collection. ebpf-go will reject maps with pins it doesn't recognize.\n   289→\ttoReplace := consumePinReplace(spec)\n   290→\n   291→\t// Attempt to load the Collection.\n   292→\tcoll, err := ebpf.NewCollectionWithOptions(spec, opts.CollectionOptions)\n   293→\n   294→\t// Collect key names of maps that are not compatible with their pinned\n   295→\t// counterparts and remove their pinning flags.\n   296→\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrMapIncompatible) {\n   297→\t\tvar incompatible []string\n   298→\t\tincompatible, err = incompatibleMaps(spec, opts.CollectionOptions)\n   299→\t\tif err != nil {\n   300→\t\t\treturn nil, nil, fmt.Errorf(\"finding incompatible maps: %w\", err)\n   301→\t\t}\n   302→\t\ttoReplace = append(toReplace, incompatible...)\n   303→\n   304→\t\t// Retry loading the Collection with necessary pinning flags removed.\n   305→\t\tcoll, err = ebpf.NewCollectionWithOptions(spec, opts.CollectionOptions)\n   306→\t}\n   307→\n   308→\t// Try to obtain the full verifier log if it was truncated. Note that\n   309→\t// VerifierError is also returned if verification was successful but the\n   310→\t// buffer was too small.\n   311→\tattempts := 5\n   312→\tfor range attempts {\n   313→\t\tvar ve *ebpf.VerifierError\n   314→\t\tif errors.As(err, &ve) && ve.Truncated {\n   315→\t\t\t// Retry with non-zero log level to avoid retrying with log disabled.\n   316→\t\t\tif opts.Programs.LogLevel == 0 {\n   317→\t\t\t\topts.Programs.LogLevel = ebpf.LogLevelBranch\n   318→\t\t\t}\n   319→\n   320→\t\t\topts.Programs.LogSize *= 4\n   321→\n   322→\t\t\t// Retry loading the Collection with increased log buffer.\n   323→\t\t\tcoll, err = ebpf.NewCollectionWithOptions(spec, opts.CollectionOptions)\n   324→\n   325→\t\t\t// Re-check error and bump attempts.\n   326→\t\t\tcontinue\n   327→\t\t}\n   328→\n   329→\t\tif err != nil {\n   330→\t\t\t// Not a VerifierError or not truncated.\n   331→\t\t\treturn nil, nil, err\n   332→\t\t}\n   333→\t}\n   334→\tif err != nil {\n   335→\t\t// Retry loop failed to resolve a VerifierError.\n   336→\t\treturn nil, nil, fmt.Errorf(\"%d-byte truncated verifier log after %d attempts: %w\", opts.CollectionOptions.Programs.LogSize, attempts, err)\n   337→\t}\n   338→\n   339→\t// Load successful, return a function that must be invoked after attaching the\n   340→\t// Collection's entrypoint programs to their respective hooks.\n   341→\tcommit := func() error {\n   342→\t\t// Commit maps that need their bpffs pins replaced.\n   343→\t\tif err := commitMapPins(toReplace, spec, coll, opts.CollectionOptions); err != nil {\n   344→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"replacing map pins on bpffs: %w\", err)\n   345→\t\t}\n   346→\t\treturn nil\n   347→\t}\n   348→\treturn coll, commit, nil\n   349→}\n   350→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. For all others like\n    34→\t\t// host devices, rely on tcx.\n    35→\t\tif device.Type() == \"netkit\" {\n    36→\t\t\tif err := upsertNetkitProgram(device, prog, progName, bpffsDir, parent); err != nil {\n    37→\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"attaching netkit program %s: %w\", progName, err)\n    38→\t\t\t}\n    39→\t\t\treturn nil\n    40→\t\t}\n    41→\n    42→\t\t// Attach using tcx if available. err != nil {\n    61→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"attaching legacy tc program %s: %w\", progName, err)\n    62→\t}\n    63→\n    64→\t// Legacy tc attached, make sure tcx is detached in case of downgrade.\n    65→\t// netkit can only be used in combination with tcx, but never legacy tc,\n    66→\t// hence for netkit detaching here would be irrelevant.\n    67→\tif err := detachGeneric(bpffsDir, progName, \"tcx\"); err != nil {\n    68→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"tcx cleanup after attaching legacy tc program %s: %w\", progName, err)\n    69→\t}\n    70→\n    71→\treturn nil\n    72→}\n    73→\n    74→func detachGeneric(bpffsDir, progName, what string) error {\n    75→\tpin := filepath.Join(bpffsDir, progName)\n    76→\terr := bpf.UnpinLink(pin)\n    77→\tif err == nil {\n    78→\t\tlog.Infof(\"Removed %s link at %s\", what, pin)\n    79→\t\treturn nil\n    80→\t}\n    81→\tif errors.Is(err, os.ErrNotExist) {\n    82→\t\treturn nil\n    83→\t}\n    84→\n    85→\t// The pinned link exists, something went wrong unpinning it.\n    86→\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unpinning %s link: %w\", what, err)\n    87→}\n    88→\n    89→// detachSKBProgram attempts to remove an existing tcx, netkit and legacy tc link\n    90→// with the given properties. Conditional Tail Call Invocation**\n\nFile: `/workspace/bpf/lib/tailcall.h`\n\n```c\n// For inline function calls when condition is false (0)\n#define __invoke_tailcall_if_0(NAME, FUNC, EXT_ERR) \\\n\tFUNC(ctx)\n\n// For tail calls when condition is true (1)\n#define __invoke_tailcall_if_1(NAME, FUNC, EXT_ERR)\t\t\\\n\t({\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\\\n\t\ttail_call_internal(ctx, NAME, EXT_ERR);\t\t\t\\\n\t})\n\n#define invoke_tailcall_if(COND, NAME, FUNC, EXT_ERR)\t\t\\\n\t__eval(__invoke_tailcall_if_, COND)(NAME, FUNC, EXT_ERR)\n```\n\n**Usage Example:**\n```c\n// /workspace/bpf/bpf_lxc.c:2203-2205\nret = invoke_tailcall_if(__and(is_defined(ENABLE_IPV4), is_defined(ENABLE_IPV6)),\n\t\t\t CILIUM_CALL_IPV4_CT_INGRESS_POLICY_ONLY,\n\t\t\t tail_ipv4_ct_ingress_policy_only, &ext_err);\n```\n\n#### **C. Internal Tail Call Handler**\n\nFile: `/workspace/bpf/lib/maps.h:290-298`\n\n```c\nstatic __always_inline __must_check int\ntail_call_internal(struct __ctx_buff *ctx, const __u32 index, __s8 *ext_err)\n{\n\ttail_call_static(ctx, CALLS_MAP, index);\n\t\n\tif (ext_err)\n\t\t*ext_err = (__s8)index;\n\treturn DROP_MISSED_TAIL_CALL;\n}\n```\n\nIf the tail call fails (index not populated), it returns `DROP_MISSED_TAIL_CALL`.\n\n---\n\n### 4. POLICY PROGRAM GENERATION (Per-Endpoint Template)\n\nFile: `/workspace/bpf/bpf_lxc.c:2178-2179`\n\n**Template policy program:**\n```c\n__section_tail(CILIUM_MAP_POLICY, TEMPLATE_LXC_ID)\nint handle_policy(struct __ctx_buff *ctx)\n{\n\t__u32 src_label = ctx_load_meta(ctx, CB_SRC_LABEL);\n\t__u32 sec_label = SECLABEL;\n\t__s8 ext_err = 0;\n\t__u16 proto;\n\tint ret;\n\t\n\tif (!validate_ethertype(ctx, &proto)) {\n\t\tret = DROP_UNSUPPORTED_L2;\n\t\tgoto out;\n\t}\n\t\n\tswitch (proto) {\n#ifdef ENABLE_IPV6\n\tcase bpf_htons(ETH_P_IPV6):\n\t\tret = invoke_tailcall_if(..., CILIUM_CALL_IPV6_CT_INGRESS_POLICY_ONLY, ...);\n\t\tsec_label = SECLABEL_IPV6;\n\t\tbreak;\n#endif\n#ifdef ENABLE_IPV4\n\tcase bpf_htons(ETH_P_IP):\n\t\tret = invoke_tailcall_if(..., CILIUM_CALL_IPV4_CT_INGRESS_POLICY_ONLY, ...);\n\t\tsec_label = SECLABEL_IPV4;\n\t\tbreak;\n#endif\n\tdefault:\n\t\tret = DROP_UNKNOWN_L3;\n\t\tbreak;\n\t}\n\t\nout:\n\tif (IS_ERR(ret))\n\t\treturn send_drop_notify_ext(ctx, src_label, sec_label, LXC_ID, ret, ext_err,\n\t\t\t\t\t    CTX_ACT_DROP, METRIC_INGRESS);\n\treturn ret;\n}\n```\n\n**Template Placeholders:**\n- `TEMPLATE_LXC_ID` → Replaced with actual endpoint ID at load time\n- `SECLABEL` → Replaced with endpoint's security label\n- `SECLABEL_IPV4` / `SECLABEL_IPV6` → Protocol-specific labels\n\n---\n\n### 7. SECTION MACRO ARCHITECTURE\n\n#### **Macro Definition Chain**\n\nFile: `/workspace/bpf/include/bpf/section.h`\n```c\n#define __section(X) __attribute__((section(X), used))\n#define __section_tail(ID, KEY) __section(__stringify(ID) \"/\" __stringify(KEY))\n#define __section_license __section(\"license\")\n#define __section_maps __section(\"maps\")\n#define __section_maps_btf __section(\".maps\")\n```\n\nThe `__section_tail` macro creates section names like `\"CILIUM_MAP_CALLS/CILIUM_CALL_IPV4_FROM_LXC\"` which maps to program index in tail call arrays.\n\n---\n\n### 3. TAIL CALL MECHANISM\n\n#### **A. Tail Call Infrastructure**\n\nFile: `/workspace/bpf/include/bpf/tailcall.h`\n\n**Assembly-level tail call:**\n```c\n#define tail_call_static(ctx_ptr, map, slot)\t\t\t\\\n{\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\\\n\tif (!__builtin_constant_p(slot))\t\t\t\\\n\t\t__throw_build_bug();\t\t\t\t\\\n\tasm volatile(\"r1 = %[ctx]\\n\\t\"\t\t\t\t\\\n\t\t\"r2 = \" __stringify(map) \" ll\\n\\t\"\t\t\\\n\t\t\"r3 = %[slot_idx]\\n\\t\"\t\t\t\t\\\n\t\t\"call 12\\n\\t\"\t\t\t\t\t\\\n\t\t:: [ctx]\"r\"(ctx_ptr), [slot_idx]\"i\"(slot)\t\\\n\t\t: \"r0\", \"r1\", \"r2\", \"r3\", \"r4\", \"r5\");\t\t\\\n}\n```\n\n**Dynamic tail call:**\n```c\nstatic __always_inline __maybe_unused void\ntail_call_dynamic(struct __ctx_buff *ctx, const void *map, __u32 slot)\n{\n\tif (__builtin_constant_p(slot))\n\t\t__throw_build_bug();\n\ttail_call(ctx, map, slot);\n}\n```\n\n#### **B. Conditional Tail Call Invocation**\n\nFile: `/workspace/bpf/lib/tailcall.h`\n\n```c\n// For inline function calls when condition is false (0)\n#define __invoke_tailcall_if_0(NAME, FUNC, EXT_ERR) \\\n\tFUNC(ctx)\n\n// For tail calls when condition is true (1)\n#define __invoke_tailcall_if_1(NAME, FUNC, EXT_ERR)\t\t\\\n\t({\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\\\n\t\ttail_call_internal(ctx, NAME, EXT_ERR);\t\t\t\\\n\t})\n\n#define invoke_tailcall_if(COND, NAME, FUNC, EXT_ERR)\t\t\\\n\t__eval(__invoke_tailcall_if_, COND)(NAME, FUNC, EXT_ERR)\n```\n\n**Usage Example:**\n```c\n// /workspace/bpf/bpf_lxc.c:2203-2205\nret = invoke_tailcall_if(__and(is_defined(ENABLE_IPV4), is_defined(ENABLE_IPV6)),\n\t\t\t CILIUM_CALL_IPV4_CT_INGRESS_POLICY_ONLY,\n\t\t\t tail_ipv4_ct_ingress_policy_only, &ext_err);\n```\n\n#### **C. Internal Tail Call Handler**\n\nFile: `/workspace/bpf/lib/maps.h:290-298`\n\n```c\nstatic __always_inline __must_check int\ntail_call_internal(struct __ctx_buff *ctx, const __u32 index, __s8 *ext_err)\n{\n\ttail_call_static(ctx, CALLS_MAP, index);\n\t\n\tif (ext_err)\n\t\t*ext_err = (__s8)index;\n\treturn DROP_MISSED_TAIL_CALL;\n}\n```\n\nIf the tail call fails (index not populated), it returns `DROP_MISSED_TAIL_CALL`.\n\n---\n\n### 4. POLICY PROGRAM GENERATION (Per-Endpoint Template)\n\nFile: `/workspace/bpf/bpf_lxc.c:2178-2179`\n\n**Template policy program:**\n```c\n__section_tail(CILIUM_MAP_POLICY, TEMPLATE_LXC_ID)\nint handle_policy(struct __ctx_buff *ctx)\n{\n\t__u32 src_label = ctx_load_meta(ctx, CB_SRC_LABEL);\n\t__u32 sec_label = SECLABEL;\n\t__s8 ext_err = 0;\n\t__u16 proto;\n\tint ret;\n\t\n\tif (!validate_ethertype(ctx, &proto)) {\n\t\tret = DROP_UNSUPPORTED_L2;\n\t\tgoto out;\n\t}\n\t\n\tswitch (proto) {\n#ifdef ENABLE_IPV6\n\tcase bpf_htons(ETH_P_IPV6):\n\t\tret = invoke_tailcall_if(..., CILIUM_CALL_IPV6_CT_INGRESS_POLICY_ONLY, ...);\n\t\tsec_label = SECLABEL_IPV6;\n\t\tbreak;\n#endif\n#ifdef ENABLE_IPV4\n\tcase bpf_htons(ETH_P_IP):\n\t\tret = invoke_tailcall_if(..., CILIUM_CALL_IPV4_CT_INGRESS_POLICY_ONLY, ...);\n\t\tsec_label = SECLABEL_IPV4;\n\t\tbreak;\n#endif\n\tdefault:\n\t\tret = DROP_UNKNOWN_L3;\n\t\tbreak;\n\t}\n\t\nout:\n\tif (IS_ERR(ret))\n\t\treturn send_drop_notify_ext(ctx, src_label, sec_label, LXC_ID, ret, ext_err,\n\t\t\t\t\t    CTX_ACT_DROP, METRIC_INGRESS);\n\treturn ret;\n}\n```\n\n**Template Placeholders:**\n- `TEMPLATE_LXC_ID` → Replaced with actual endpoint ID at load time\n- `SECLABEL` → Replaced with endpoint's security label\n- `SECLABEL_IPV4` / `SECLABEL_IPV6` → Protocol-specific labels\n\n---\n\n### 7. CUSTOM PROGRAM FRAMEWORK\n\nFile: `/workspace/bpf/custom/bpf_custom.c`\n\n**Template system for user-defined programs:**\n\n```c\n// Define custom implementation\n#ifndef BPF_CUSTOM_PROG_FILE\n#define BPF_CUSTOM_PROG_FILE bytecount.h\n#endif\n\n#ifndef BPF_CUSTOM_PROG_NAME\n#define BPF_CUSTOM_PROG_NAME custom\n#endif\n\n#include STRINGIFY(BPF_CUSTOM_PROG_FILE)\n\n__section(STRINGIFY(BPF_CUSTOM_PROG_NAME))\nint custom_hook(const struct __ctx_buff *ctx)\n{\n    __u32 custom_meta = ctx_load_meta(ctx, CB_CUSTOM_CALLS);\n    __u32 identity = custom_meta & 0xffffff;\n    int ret = (custom_meta >> 24) & 0xff;\n    \n    // Call user-defined function\n    custom_prog(ctx, identity);\n    \n    // Return action selected by parent\n    return ret;\n}\n```\n\n**Invocation from main program:**\nFile: `/workspace/bpf/bpf_lxc.c:2140-2152`\n\n```c\n#ifdef ENABLE_CUSTOM_CALLS\n\tif (!proxy_redirect &&\n\t    !encode_custom_prog_meta(ctx, ret, src_sec_identity)) {\n\t\ttail_call_static(ctx, CUSTOM_CALLS_MAP,\n\t\t\t\t CUSTOM_CALLS_IDX_IPV4_INGRESS);\n\t\tupdate_metrics(ctx_full_len(ctx), METRIC_INGRESS,\n\t\t\t       REASON_MISSED_CUSTOM_CALL);\n\t}\n#endif\n```\n\n---\n\n### 15. PRACTICAL SUBSYSTEM INTEGRATION EXAMPLES\n\n#### **A. IPSec Integration Pattern**\n\nSearch for `ENABLE_IPSEC` flags throughout bpf/ directory:\n- Conditional encryption/decryption hooks\n- Tunnel establishment tracking\n- Per-flow IPSec state management\n\n#### **B. NodePort Load Balancing**\n\nFile: `/workspace/bpf/lib/nodeport.h`\n- Multiple tail calls for ingress NAT, egress NAT, DSR variants\n- Conditional compilation based on DSR_ENCAP_MODE\n- Reverse NAT for return traffic\n\n#### **C. Egress Gateway**\n\nPattern:\n- Intercepts egress traffic\n- Applies routing rules\n- Can modify destination MAC/IP\n- Integrated via conditional compilation\n\n---\n\n### SUMMARY: KEY ARCHITECTURAL PRINCIPLES\n\n1. **Hierarchical Tail Calls:** Main entry points dispatch to feature-specific tail-called programs\n2. **Template-Based Generation:** Programs parameterized at compile-time with endpoint IDs\n3. **Map-Based Configuration:** All per-endpoint state stored in pinned BPF maps\n4. **Conditional Compilation:** Features enabled/disabled at compile time via -D flags\n5. **Dual Hook Support:** TC (more flexible) and XDP (faster) can both be attached\n6. **Program Type Abstraction:** Context type (SKB/XDP/Sock) abstracted via header macros\n7. **Shared Maps:** Multiple programs access same maps for state coordination\n8. **Error Handling:** Non-zero returns trigger drop notifications with error codes\n\nThis architecture enables Cilium to support 50+ different processing hooks while maintaining a unified codebase across different network contexts (container, host, overlay, etc.)."}],"totalDurationMs":105943,"totalTokens":83442,"totalToolUseCount":41,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1496,"cache_read_input_tokens":74612,"output_tokens":7333,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1496,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}}}

[Purpose](#1-purpose)\n2. [Dependencies](#2-dependencies)\n3. [Relevant Components](#3-relevant-components)\n4. [Failure Modes](#4-failure-modes)\n5. [Testing](#5-testing)\n6. [Debugging](#6-debugging)\n7. [Adding a New Hook](#7-adding-a-new-hook)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Purpose\n\n### What Problem Does the eBPF Datapath Solve?\n\nThe eBPF datapath is the **core execution engine** that implements Cilium's networking and security policies at the kernel level. It solves several critical problems:\n\n1. **High-Performance Policy Enforcement:** Traditional iptables-based firewalls have linear lookup performance and can't efficiently express complex policy logic. The eBPF datapath executes policy checks in kernel space with O(1) or O(log n) map lookups, avoiding expensive context switches between kernel and userspace.\n\n2. **Dynamic Network Policy:** Cilium uses identity-based (rather than IP-based) policies. The eBPF datapath performs real-time policy lookups against dynamically updated maps as endpoints join/leave the cluster, without requiring userspace packet interception.\n\n3. **Transparent Service Mesh:** eBPF socket-level hooks (`cgroup/connect4`, `cgroup/sendmsg4`, etc. in `bpf_sock.c`) enable transparent load-balancing and service mesh without requiring sidecar proxies, reducing latency and resource overhead.\n\n4. **In-Kernel NAT and Load-Balancing:** Rather than delegating to userspace proxies, the datapath implements SNAT, DNAT, and load-balancing directly in eBPF programs (via `lib/nat.h` and `lib/lb.h`).\n\n5. **Encryption and Tunneling:** The datapath handles IPSec encryption, WireGuard integration, and VXLAN overlays entirely in-kernel via conditional eBPF programs.\n\n6. **Connection Tracking:** Maintains stateful firewall capabilities with TCP connection state tracking in kernel BPF maps, enabling asymmetric policies based on connection direction.\n\n### Why eBPF Instead of Traditional Approaches?\n\n| Approach | Latency | Flexibility | Integration | Memory |\n|----------|---------|-------------|-------------|--------|\n| **iptables** | 10-100µs per rule | Limited policy logic | Kernel tables only | Large (many rules) |\n| **userspace proxies** | 100-1000µs (context switch) | Highly flexible | Application layer | Very high (process overhead) |\n| **eBPF datapath** | <1µs (in-kernel) | Extensible via tail calls | Kernel + userspace coordination | Minimal (map-based) |\n\neBPF provides a **programmable kernel** without:\n- Kernel recompilation (dynamic loading)\n- Userspace context switches (in-kernel execution)\n- Hard-coded features (tail calls allow dynamic program composition)\n- Performance penalties (kernel-level operation)\n\n### Key Responsibilities\n\nThe eBPF datapath subsystem is responsible for:\n\n1. **Network Policy Enforcement:** Filtering packets based on security identities and L3/L4 rules\n2. **Service Load-Balancing:** Distributing traffic across endpoints (ClusterIP, NodePort, ExternalIP)\n3. **NAT (Network Address Translation):** SNAT for egress, DNAT for ingress traffic\n4. **Connection Tracking:** Stateful firewall with TCP state machine\n5. **Endpoint Routing:** Routing packets between containers/VMs and the host/network\n6. **Tunneling & Encapsulation:** VXLAN overlays, IPSec, WireGuard integration\n7. **L7 Proxy Integration:** Redirecting traffic to userspace Envoy proxy when needed\n8. **Metrics & Monitoring:** Collecting per-packet statistics and debug events\n\n### Integration with Kubernetes Networking\n\n```\nUser Container → Linux Network Stack\n    ↓\n[TC Ingress Hook] cil_from_container (bpf_lxc.c)\n    ↓\n[Policy Check] POLICY_CALL_MAP → per-endpoint policy program\n    ↓\n[Identity Lookup] ipcache map → source security label\n    ↓\n[Route Lookup] ENDPOINTS_MAP → destination endpoint location\n    ↓\n[NAT/LB] SNAT_MAPPING, LB*_SERVICES_MAP\n    ↓\n[Tunnel Encapsulation] (if overlay) → kernel stack\n    ↓\nPhysical NIC → Remote Pod via Kubernetes network fabric\n```\n\nThe datapath seamlessly bridges:\n- **Container endpoints** (network namespaces) ↔ **Host network** (kernel)\n- **Pod-to-pod communication** ↔ **Pod-to-service communication**\n- **Kubernetes service abstraction** (ClusterIP, NodePort) ↔ **Actual endpoints**\n\n---\n\n## 2. Dependencies\n\n### Internal Dependencies: Upstream (What Calls the Datapath)\n\n**Control Plane → Datapath:**\n- `/workspace/pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` (EndpointManager) → Triggers endpoint program generation and loading when policies change\n- `/workspace/pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` (Loader) → Main orchestrator for program compilation and attachment\n- `/workspace/pkg/daemon/daemon.go` (Cilium daemon) → Coordinates policy updates and datapath reloads\n- `/workspace/pkg/identity/identity.go` → Provides security identity labels used in policy decisions\n- `/workspace/pkg/policy/policy.go` → Computes network policies, passed to datapath for enforcement\n\n**Configuration Flows:**\n1. Endpoint created → `/workspace/pkg/endpoint/endpoint.go` → calls `endpoint.Regenerate()` → triggers `/workspace/pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:Reinitialize()`\n2. Policy changed → `/workspace/pkg/policy/repository.go` → notifies all affected endpoints → triggers regeneration\n3. Service added → `/workspace/pkg/service/service.go` → updates LB maps (`/workspace/pkg/maps/lbmap/`) → datapath picks up changes\n\n### Internal Dependencies: Downstream (What the Datapath Calls)\n\n**Datapath → Support Systems:**\n- `/workspace/pkg/maps/` (Map management) → Provides map lifecycle (create, update, delete, cleanup)\n  - `policymap/` - Policy enforcement maps\n  - `nat/` - NAT translation maps\n  - `lbmap/` - Load balancer maps\n  - `ctmap/` - Connection tracking maps\n  - `ipcache/` - IP-to-identity cache\n  - `lxcmap/` - Endpoint information maps\n\n- `/workspace/pkg/bpf/` (eBPF wrapper library)\n  - `collection.go` - Loads ELF files, handles verifier errors\n  - `map_linux.go` - Per-CPU maps, caching, sync retry logic\n  - `bpffs_linux.go` - BPF filesystem pinning/unpinning\n\n- `/workspace/pkg/sysctl/` → Configures kernel parameters (e.g., `net.ipv4.conf.*.rp_filter`, `net.ipv4.ip_forward`)\n\n- `/workspace/pkg/netlink/` → Low-level netlink operations for TC filter attachment, device enumeration\n\n- `/workspace/pkg/monitor/` → Reports debug events and metrics back to Cilium agent for monitoring\n\n### Kernel API Dependencies\n\n**BPF System Calls:**\n- `bpf(BPF_PROG_LOAD)` - Load eBPF programs into kernel (via `pkg/bpf/collection.go`)\n- `bpf(BPF_MAP_CREATE)` - Create BPF maps (via `pkg/maps/`)\n- `bpf(BPF_OBJ_PIN)` / `bpf(BPF_OBJ_GET)` - Pin/unpin objects to BPF filesystem (via `pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go`)\n\n**Netlink Protocol:**\n- `RTM_NEWQDISC` / `RTM_DELQDISC` - Create/delete qdisc (clsact) for TC\n- `RTM_NEWTFILTER` / `RTM_DELTFILTER` - Attach/detach TC filters (via `pkg/datapath/loader/tc.go`)\n- `RTM_NEWLINK` / `RTM_GETLINK` - Interface enumeration and XDP attachment (via `pkg/datapath/loader/xdp.go`)\n\n**Cgroup v2 APIs:**\n- `BPF_PROG_ATTACH` to `/dev/cgroup/...` - Attach socket programs (via `bpf_sock.c`)\n\n**BPF Program Types:**\n- `BPF_PROG_TYPE_SCHED_CLS` - TC programs (main datapath)\n- `BPF_PROG_TYPE_XDP` - XDP early filtering\n- `BPF_PROG_TYPE_CGROUP_SOCK_ADDR` - Socket address policy hooks\n- `BPF_PROG_TYPE_SK_MSG` - Socket message handling\n\n**BPF Map Types:**\n- `BPF_MAP_TYPE_HASH` - Endpoint lookup, service lookup\n- `BPF_MAP_TYPE_LRU_HASH` - Connection tracking, NAT (auto-eviction)\n- `BPF_MAP_TYPE_LPM_TRIE` - Policy (prefix matching), IP cache (CIDR matching)\n- `BPF_MAP_TYPE_PROG_ARRAY` - Tail call maps (program composition)\n- `BPF_MAP_TYPE_PERCPU_HASH` - Metrics (per-CPU counters)\n\n**BPF Helpers Used:**\n- `bpf_map_lookup_elem()` - Read from maps (policy, endpoint, NAT, etc.)\n- `bpf_map_update_elem()` - Write to maps (connection tracking, metrics)\n- `bpf_tail_call()` - Jump to next eBPF program\n- `bpf_redirect()` - Redirect packet to interface\n- `bpf_clone_redirect()` - Duplicate packet to interface\n- `bpf_perf_event_output()` - Send trace/debug events\n- `bpf_get_current_pid_tgid()` - Get process ID (socket programs)\n- `bpf_probe_read()` - Read kernel memory safely\n\n### External/Ecosystem Dependencies\n\n- **Cilium CLI** (`cilium-cli`) → Uses datapath for policy validation\n- **Kubernetes CNI plugin** → Invokes Cilium binary for pod networking setup\n- **NetworkPolicy/CiliumNetworkPolicy** CRDs → Converted to datapath policies\n- **etcd/Consul** → Stores policy state, retrieved by control plane\n- **Monitoring systems** (Prometheus, etc.) → Consume datapath metrics via `/metrics`\n\n### Go ↔ C Boundary\n\nThe datapath exists at a critical **Go-to-C transition point:**\n\n```\nGo Control Plane\n    ↓\nPolicy Resolution (Go)\n    ↓\n[BOUNDARY: pkg/datapath/loader/]\n    ↓\nC Program Generation & Compilation (C + clang)\n    ↓\nELF Object Loading (bpf() syscalls)\n    ↓\nKernel eBPF Execution (Kernel-only)\n    ↓\n[BOUNDARY: bpf maps, netlink updates]\n    ↓\nGo Runtime Observability (metrics, monitoring)\n```\n\n**Data Exchange Mechanisms:**\n1. **Configuration Headers:** Go generates `lxc_config.h`, `node_config.h`, etc. with C #define macros (see `pkg/datapath/loader/template.go`)\n2. **BPF Maps:** Shared memory regions created by Go, read/written by both Go and eBPF programs\n3. **Netlink Events:** Go sends TC filter updates, eBPF programs are attached/detached\n4. **Debug Events:** eBPF programs output trace data via perf buffers, Go reads and logs them\n\n---\n\n## 3.
